--- 帖子 #809 ---
Most people who post their trade results in this forum do so with the intent of sharing the experience to help others,and learn from others, like yourself.   Sometimes they share a bad trade in order to get feed back on what they did wrong and how to correct the errors made.  Other times they share good trades which resulted in a goodly number of pips being banked.

I look to learn from others results both positive and negative and their methods.  If someone has banked 70 plus pips on a trade,...I want to know how they did it.  If it is a setup I am not familiar with, then I want to examine it and see if integrating a system might better my trading style.

I started trading commodities part time in 2001, but I never really enjoyed trading in that venue.  When I discovered forex in 2003, I switched and went full time in the Forex market in late 2004.  My philosophy has always been to take small profits and when able increase the amount of lots traded. (Slow but steady.)

I have been following this thread since Lever started it.  I have back tested it, then and forward tested it until I was satisfied it fit my style of trading.  Once I have decided which currency pair to trade for the day, I use the four TF Cornflower system to decide when to enter the trade.

I live on the West Coast of the U.S. and trade both the Asian and London sessions.  This morning during the London session, I determined that the GBP/JPY was going to continue on it's South bound journey.  Using Cornflower I placed a sell at 236.72.  The run started to end at 236.20.  By the time I decided it was ending, I closed with a profit of 40 pips (my initial goal was only 20 pips.)

Upon preparing to trade the Asian session this afternoon, I was surprised to find the GBP/JPY had dropped to 234.12.  While I was happy with the 40 pip profit from the earlier trade, my first thought was, is there anything I could have done to have banked some of the 220 pips I left on the table.  After careful thought (and several cups of coffee) I saw where I could improve my results.

Firstly, when I closed the trade, it was quite apparent that price had begun an upward climb on the 5M chart.  Instead of closing the trade, I should have noticed my option to use my trading station's close and reverse option and banked some of the pips on the retracement (it finally topped out at 237.14.)

Second, I had focused my attention on the 5M chart ONLY (a habit left over from my scalping days.)  Because price was choppy on the 5M chart, I decided another trade would not be viable.  If I had looked at the H, 30M, and 15M charts, I would have seen the trend was intact and my choppy 5M chart was only price taking a breather.

Third,  If I had looked at the other charts, I could have placed another sell order with a trailing stop and gone to bed secure in the knowledge that I had already banked pips for the day, and the trade was covered by the stop. An observation I will not miss again.

I decided to share this trade not to boast of my 40 pip profit, but to share my mistakes in analyzing the charts.  Hopefully it will prevent someone else from missing an opportunity like the one I missed today.

The venerable Peter Bain has said trading the Forex Market is like going to war.  It's you against the other guy, and he more than likely has more experience, is better informed,....and wants your lunch!  I am happy I banked those 40 pips and that my errors in evaluating the market only cost me unrealized profits (for those interested, I now trade 25 lots at $.84 per lot, or approximately $21.00 per pip) and not the hard earned money in the trading account.

Trading the Forex is a great business.  However, it is terribly unforgiving of any ignorance, carelessness or neglect, (the same mantra I have when I fly an aircraft).  Learning from other people's mistakes and successes will help to shorten the learning curve.

While the object of trading is to make money,....It's not how much money you make,....but what you do with the money after you make it that counts. Family, Passion, and Live Well.

Clansman

You then drop to the 30M chart and again, no pullbacks.  Not only are there no pullbacks, but there's DISTANCE between the high or low of the bar and the 8 EMA.  Drop to the 15M and it's still a runaway Piptrain.  No pullbacks in sight, how to take advantage of this moneymaker?  Well, I've found that in these times there is no reason to not be making money in an obvious market move.  Just drop down to the 5M and 1M charts in those circumstances and play those timeframes Cornflower style exactly the same as if they were the 1H chart.  What I'm saying is that there is always a timeframe to play Cornflower on in a trending market.  Just find the one that has shown a couple pullbacks to the 12/24 area and then wait for the next opportunity to get in.  You have to keep a vigilant eye on your stops, as always, but as long as you do, you've got an 80% chance of winning which is HUGE.

--- 帖子 #819 ---
Thanks Matrixxdg.

I understand, it is especially frustrating when your stop is hit and price then turns around and proceeds to move another 20 to 30 pips before finally stalling out.  I prefer to keep my stop line in my head while I am trading (I find it allows for more flexibility when price starts to fluctuate.)    If there is a strong trend and price is moving well, I keep a 30 pip margin in my head.    If it is ranging, I use 20 pips on either side of the channel.   I follow the 5M and 15M charts when it is ranging.   I use pivot points and support and resistance lines, and I watch carefully around those areas (it is amazing how often a Cornflower pullback happens around those areas.)

If I have a trade that is in the positive and I am going to be away from the computer, I set my stop half way between where price is and my break even point, assuring some profit.   When I use a trailing stop, I set it anywhere between 30 pips and 100 pips behind price (depends on the particular currency and the movement at the time.)   If I am sure price will continue on a trend, but I can't gauge where it might retrace to before continuing, I will set a higher trailing stop.    Unfortunately, trading is part art and part science....more art than science.

I hope the above is useful.

BTW,....I am MacGregor as well!!!

--- 帖子 #828 ---
I tried a couple of scalps today on Cable, and I thought I'd show you how I avoided what could have been a bad trade.  Pretty basic stuff, but then there's a lot of new people coming on all the time, isn't there?

I got in for a nice scalp of 26 pips where you can see the labels.  I exited this trade sharpish after the long lower shadow gave an indication that the bears where fighting back.  Sure enough, the price started rising rapidly, and I was waiting for it to stall at any of the MA lines.  In the meantime, I drew a trend line from the first black arrow to see if it would prove to show resistance to the rising price.  Obviously, it didn't, and the price didn't stop until it hit the 50sma.  Now, of course, my trend line had the potential to be a support, so I waited to see what would happen.  I watched the price drop through 3 MA's until it came to a grinding halt at my trend line, where the second black arrow is pointing. The next candlestick proved to be a hammer, just above the M1 line indicating a reversal and so it proved.   A simple trend line saved me a lot of grief.   Magic, eh?

--- 帖子 #839 ---
In forex trading like everything else, you have to pay your dues (sometimes quite literally if you are not careful.)  I crashed my first forex account and did serious damage to the second before I developed the style that worked for me.

While I can't tell you what will work for you,....I can share what I did on my road to surviving the forex market.

My first goal was to be consistent in my trading (seven successful trades out of ten was my goal.)  Next I had to decide how much risk I was willing to live with, as well as, a nonemotional, mechanical, way to increase the number of lots in my trades. I did that by setting up an excel spread sheet with the following headings; # Lots, Stop pips, Margin, Total Margin Required, Trade Profit, Draw, To Account, Balance.   Once the formulas are tied in, you can see the potential risk for your trades.  There are only three places you can make changes in the formulas, Beginning Balance, # Lots, and Draw.  All columns with the exception of the # Lots column (which is a straight number) are in dollars .  I'll dig up an example and post it soon.

When a change is made in the the # Lots column, all columns with the exception of the Draw column are changed.

The Total Margin Required column is the combined total of the Stop Pips and Margin columns.

The Stop Pips column is the number of pips your stop is set to in dollars. It is the most important in my mind. It tells you in dollars how much you will be risking for the number of lots you want to trade.  I prefer to look at dollars vs percentages when evaluating my risk (i.e. $1,000.00 is more sobering to me than say 2%.)   I also use my balance  in determining the number of lots to trade.  The spread sheet holds forty-four trades with increasing lots as you move down the page.  If I experience a loss, I look to the balance on the spread sheet that is the closest amount below my actual account and place my next trade using the # of lots indicated.

The draw column is the amount you pull from the account to pay yourself.

I have one sheet for the EUR/USD and GBP/USD (since those currencies are in even dollars) and one for GBP/JPY, USD/CHF, USD/JPY, which are approximately $0.85 per pip.

I decided to setup a corporation for my trading account.  Some people had said to me that a corporation is a lot of extra paper work for just one person.  However, I preferred the benefits of a corporation.  The corporation pays me biweekly and takes my taxes out of my check just like any other paycheck.  The company has different tax advantages than I do as an individual.  The most important reason in my mind, for setting up a corporation is....it's cleaner.  Everything is documented and above board.

If my ramblings have not answered your question,..I hope they have at least pointed you to the road best suited to you.

Trade well...live well.

--- 帖子 #882 ---
Hello mate, and first of all, well done for actually having the nerve to admit to all and sundry that you've been through this thread 3 times yet the method still mystifies you. A lot of newbies out there wouldn't have had the balls to do that, mate, quite honestly, and they'd have moved on to something else by now. So give yourself a pat on the back!

As for the method itself......the best thing about Cornflower is that, once you understand the simple rules, you can adapt it to your own way of trading. It's so versatile, I kid you not. The original rules basically say to trade pull-backs on the 1H charts and break-outs on the 30m charts, which gives you a good start. You can trade pull-backs after price has touched 24ema, 12ema or 8ema, depending on how fast and strong the trend is. A strong trend often gives the price no time to retrace to the 12ema, never mind the 24ema, before it's off again on its travels. So at time likes that, you have to be really on the ball to spot a pull-back to the 8ema. However, when the trade is a bit more pedestrian, then a nice pull-back to the 12 or the 24 is just the ticket to prepare you for entering what could be a nice trade.

On the 30min chart, watch for what looks like a trend change. The 8, 12 and 24, will all show signs of reversing, and when they do and cross the 72, that's your break-out, and a clear opportunity for a nice long or short trade, depending on direction.

I know that Felicia doesn't recommend this, but you CAN do all this on the 15min charts as well, but if she doesn't recommend it, then you can be sure that there's a good reason. However, by her own admission, it CAN be scalped on the 5min and the 1min charts, and I've proved that to myself just lately by joining in the action. Fast and furious, but a lot of fun!

Anyway, mate, just thought I'd offer you my own view on all this, but in the end, it's down to you and you alone how you handle it. It's a great system.....stick with it, adapt to it, and you'll never regret it, I promise.

Nevertheless, PLEASE read the pdf we've all been on about. It's an artform in itself!   Also, try and study as many charts as possible that people have posted, and try working out WHY they did what they did.   Best of luck, mate.

Cheers

--- 帖子 #889 ---
Hello again, mate.

My thoughts on this one is that it's always best to wait to see what the next candle is going to do.   You may get the price heading towards the 12 or the 24ema and sometimes it'll come to a grinding halt right on the MA, with the next candle showing signs of a definite reversal, which is what you want.  Other times, the next candle could carry merrily on in the same direction, crossing towards the 72ema.   At times like that, you have to wait for the price to come back across the 24ema before entering the trade.  Of course, nothing is guaranteed, but if it's gone into the 24-72 zone and reversed, then it's starting to look likely that it's going to provide a nice little trade.

Really, it's all about one's own judgement.  Watch the candles and try and read what they're tellling you.  With the Cornflower system, you don't need any indicators other than the candles, the MA's and (for me, at least) pivot points, with the odd trend line thrown in now and again.   Pivot points stop me from entering trades with bad Risk/Reward Ratios, but at the same time, give me clear targets to work towards.

Works for me, mate, and it'll work for you, once you've got a routine established.

Cheers

--- 帖子 #898 ---
Hello mate.

It looks as if you're getting there. However, just a couple of comments. Waiting for the next candle to close is up to you, mate. Some do and some don't. It's purely a matter of choice. The purists will tell you that waiting is the correct thing to do, but others will say no, get on board ASAP! My advice is to judge each case on its merits, and act accordingly. If the signals all look right to you, and you're feeling confident about the trade, then go for it. Otherwise, stay out and watch, entering only when you feel at ease with your decision. What is right or wrong to YOU is the only thing that matters when it comes right down to it.

Your end comments regarding using smaller TF's to pin-point entries is spot on. You're further along than you think, mate!

I'd like to suggest that you study all the charts you can get hold of, mate, so you can see where other people succeeded or failed. Go back to the "Trading Systems" page, scroll down to where "Cornflower 1hr method" is, and you'll see a little paper-clip. Click on that, and a new window will open with all the attachments that people have submitted since the thread began. LOADS of charts, I promise you! Study them and learn.

Take care, mate, and keep on keepin' on.

Cheers

--- 帖子 #913 ---
Hello Apume,

Out of respect for Lever, I am a bit hesitant to discuss other trading ideas on the Cornflower thread.  That being said, I believe I can state how I blend the Cornflower system into my trading psyche.

First I would recommend you read the following threads here on the forum;

Jacko's Forex house of pleasure and pain.  The first page really gives you his system in a nutshell, however I highly recommend reading the entire thread.

Second read Phillip Nel's 5Min Intraday System.

How I trade.  When I am deciding which pairs to trade, I put up three charts; Daily, Hourly, and 15M.  Each chart has the four Cornflower ema's 8,12,24, and 72 (weighted more heavily towards the most recent price action.)  I also have a MACD with the standard default settings of 12,26,9.  Before we go any farther,  Let me make one thing clear about the MACD...I use the MACD for divergence only.  It is a lagging indicator and cannot be used to make entry decisions.   OK,....now that I have that out of the way, here's how I analyze the charts.  I start with the Daily.  First I look at the trend and the Cornflower trend to see the long term direction.  Next I look for divergence between price action and MACD, and the Histogram.  Divergence in the MACD or its Histogram may indicate a new direction for price.  I also look to see if there are any telltale candle patterns such as a new high or low, double top or bottom, head and shoulders, triangle, etc..  After finishing the Daily, I move to the Hourly chart.  I then go through the same procedure I did on the Daily chart.  After finishing the Hourly chart, I move to the 15M chart.  I do the same on the 15M chart as I did on the Daily and the Hourly charts.  However, I also take into consideration where price is in relation to my pivot points on the 15M chart.  I do this with all the pairs I follow.  When I am watching for a trade opportunity, I watch the 5M and 15M charts, since a retracement will start with the lower TF charts.  Once I see a retracement starting on the 5M and 15M charts, I then begin paying more attention to the 30M chart.  Depending on how it looks, I will either trade off the 30M chart or wait for the retracement on the Hourly chart.  Once you develop the feel for the Cornflower system, I believe you will find it to be a very solid trading system.

While I cannot tell you what will work for you, I hope the above is useful in your search for your own way.  One last thing,....trading the Forex is part art, part science,........and its more art than science.

Good luck on your learning curve,...may it be swift and profitable.

--- 帖子 #919 ---
Hey Bunton,

I use the Cornflower 8,12,24,and 72 ema's on my 5M chart.  Retracements start to happen on the lower time frame charts.  I use the 15M charts for trade entries and exits (less whipsaws.)  I use the 5M charts to clarify any rapid price action on the 15M charts.  One of the things I look for is a consistency of the ema's between the Hourly, 30M, 15M, and 5M charts.  I also use my pivot points to see where price is on the charts (pivot points are like working with a topo map...it lets you see the terrain in advance.)

Hope that helps.

--- 帖子 #920 ---
When I started trading, I had a day job (one that required I work a 12 hour day and be on call 24/7 to handle any client problems) and was only able to do one trade a day.  I now trade full time.  Yes I am a day trader now, however, I have been looking into switching into long term trades.

I live on the West Coast as well.  I trade the Asian and London sessions.  Tokyo opens at 1600 PT and London at 0000 PT.  The Asian session is not as volatile as the London session.  There is action around the London session opening most days (usually around 2300 PT to 0100 PT.)  Another active time is between 0500 PT and 0900 PT.

Hi,

Just wanted to add my small input which I use with this setup just to give me exit and re-enter points to gain the most of a trend.

I added the "Signal Line" indecator. I enter with the rules of the CF on the Hour and keep an eye on the "Signal Line" on the 30min for any change in direction. When in a Long trade, I'll TP and exit at the change in direction on the signal line on 30min (color change should stay for at least one candle).

I'll wait until price bounces from any EMA and "re-enter" again.

--- 帖子 #938 ---
Slow weekend... kind of bored, so I'll stop lurking and come out of the bushes and I'll try taking a crack at this question...

This system doesn't react to EMA crosses.  It reacts to price action in relation to EMAs and uses EMA position to dictate trend.  While it's true that short EMAs crossing up through the 72 EMA would signal the beginning of an uptrend, nothing is done unless price action confirms a bullish move (i.e. a strong bull candle on the 30 min chart piercing the 72 EMA with the other EMAs above the 72 EMA would be an aggressive buy signal)

As I interpret it, there is no "indicator" that encompasses this system.  In fact, this system is an indicator free system that is controlled by price action and trend, with all signals being based on price action alone.  I have no idea what the "signal line indicator" is, so I could be wrong, but you really don't need an indicator to make this system work for you.

If you're still not getting this, I suggest you reread the posts again... slowly... (especially the ones written by Felicia) because I think they are VERY clearly written.

That aside, I'd like to thank Felicia for reintroducing me to a slightly more "purist" method of trading.  It's been years since I've started trading and somewhere along the way, I found a path that led me away from my "purist" trading methods and started relying on indicators to make decisions for me.  After finding this thread, I've regained my interest in watching price bars and am going back to my old ways.  Cheers!

--- 帖子 #948 ---
Hi fx_ninja. The nature of the system requires that the EMAs be on the price graph. How would you know the price has pulled back to the 12ema if the EMAs are on a separate window? Sure, a separate window would show the trend, but you wouldn't know where to enter.

The best advice for trading Cornflower is Patience. One of the people in my chatroom sometimes doesn't take a CF trade for days, just waiting for the perfect setup, then he goes and takes several hundred pips in one go at the end of the week, then goes off grinning like a Cheshire Cat to count his money.

This week it was the jpy pairs. Friday was a bit of a CF goldmine. I took 225 pips myself on u/j, e/j and g/j. I could have got more, but I wasn't quick enough to grab entries on the other jpy pairs.

To maximise profit is simple. Just wait for the properly stacked EMAs at 30-60 degrees to show up, then just trade the pullbacks.

--- 帖子 #976 ---
Hi All,

I have been using the cornflower for awhile and doing very well. I have the ability to trade during the day and was looking for a Intraday type style.

Well here is what I have been using for the past 2 weeks with great success and thought I would share.

I am using the cornflower setup on a 10 minute chart with the following criteria:

Set up a 10M chart with the Cornflower EMA’s

On your chart, set an alert to signal when the 24 ema crosses the 8 ema AND a second alert when the 8 ema crosses the 72 ema. This covers all of your bases.

For a successful trade, make sure the 8, 12, 24 ema’s are moving in the direction of the move with about a 20% angle or more. The more aggressive the angle of the ema’s the better the possibility of a successful trade and no reversal.

Also, the candle has to be moving UP or DOWN aggressively. The crossing of the 8ema and the 24ema will happen almost immediately at the beginning of the new move.

I ride the move until I see the first close of a red candle on the BUY or a green candle on the SELL, then I get out. Or, I use the RENKO chart to determine when the move has stopped.(Not allot of charting packages have RENKO, mine does, and I love it)

I know this is not how cornflower was originally designed by Lever70, but it's working for me for intraday trading.

MG

http://www.tradecore.us/images/audjpy.gif

--- 帖子 #992 ---
Of all the indicators out there, the MACD is closest to price because it is a function of the distance between moving averages.  My beef with it is its tendency to lag price action.  However, Alexander Elder has made a good case for the power of MACD divergences on longer-term charts.  Though I am averse to indicators, if something shows promise I will not dismiss it out of hand.

Phillip Nel has a very nice 4H system based on the 5-13-1 MACD.  I suggest reading up on it.  There might be a way to combine his insights with Cornflower into something that is tradeable.  However, I am not sure what you're doing with the other MACD.  It appears to mimic the action of the shorter moving averages on the chart.

--- 帖子 #994 ---
That is exactly what it means.

The best trends are indicated by a nice liftoff or descent of the short EMAs from the 72 EMA.  If the angle of separation is not clearly visible, then we have stagnant price action, and a lower-probability setup.  I do not take trades unless the short EMAs have clearly separated from the 72 EMA.  When we get the inevitable pullback, we should have a clearly identifiable trend in place.  These are the only conditions under which we should take a CF trade.  NOT when the short EMAs have yet to cross over the 72 EMA, or when they have kinda sorta crossed.  Don't guess and don't force trades.  Wait for the best entries.

--- 帖子 #998 ---
Thanks bunton.  It's not too often I get a trade that runs that long.  It sure feels good when they do.

MACD stands for Moving Average Convergence / Divergence.  It shows the difference between a fast and slow ema (set to close.)  It also has an ema which is the signal line.  The standard settings are 12 (fast ema,) 26 (slow ema.) and 9 (signal line.)  Another component is the histogram.  It is there to help show when the MACD and signal lines are crossing.

MACD is designed to show trend changes, however, it is really too slow to be used in forex trading.  I use it for divergence and histogram divergence.  For example, divergence happens when price action makes a new high and MACD is heading the other direction.  This indicates that there is the possibility that the upward trend is slowing down and maybe turning.

I posted a link for Answers.com.  Click on the link and type MACD in the search window, and it will give you more detailed information.

http://www.answers.com/

Regards,

--- 帖子 #1008 ---
I guess we are all too busy making money

In reality, the system needs no additions to work. All you need to do is develop the patience, and the willpower to trade only strong setups and avoid the weak ones or making trades, just to be in the market.

In recent weeks, I have discovered 2 nice pairs to trade CF with.

First is GBP/NZD. Despite the usually horrendous spread of around 30-35 pips at most brokers that even carry this pair, the results can be enormous.

Use a 100pip stop, targets 300-500 pips, move stop to break even at +70-+80, trail 120pips or greater. This is a fantastic pair to trade and in my opinion, the only way to trade NZD.

The second pair is GBP/CAD. With a much nicer spread of 10 pips, this one can also pick up a great number of pips. Also, with CAD being such a nice trending currency, you can pick up long runs using Cornflower. Anywhere from 100-300 pips per day is possible with this pair.

Try both pairs on demo for a couple of weeks to get a feel for them. I think you will agree they are quite remarkable.

--- 帖子 #1031 ---
Hey Quickdraw.

In answer to your scalping question, I have been watching and demo-ing both 1m and 5m charts with Cornflower and found them to be very much "do-able"!

The MA's are different from the longer TF's, but I have found that they lend themselves very nicely to scalping. Felicia, by her own admission, likes scalping, but says that Cornflower is intended primarily to be used with the 30m chart (trading breakouts), and the 1H chart (trading pull-backs). At least, that's how I've interpreted her instructions.

To be honest, I've been using both the above ways of trading on the 1m and the 5m charts, usually aiming for around 10 pips at a time, or aiming for the next Pivot line. As with most trading, it's not just taking any trade that comes along, but watching for what could be identified as a high-probability trades. In other words, stick to the basic Cornflower rules, even on these smaller TF's and you'll soon spot the opportunities if you have the patience. These results, by the way, are from trading Cable, as I've found it to be ideal for this type of trading. Even on a quiet day, Cable usually supplies some nice scalping trades.

Anyway, the only way you're going to find out if it's for you, is to jump in and try it, mate. Best of luck.

Cheers

Though they may seem like large stops, you can't have large gains without attendant risk.  And position-sizing and money management are very important.

By the way posting charts is fairly simple.

First: right click on your chart and from the menu select "save as picture"

Second: select "active chart (as is)" then click on "save"

Third: select the paper clip symbol in the menu above this active window and a new window will open that has a couple of "browse buttons" which permit you to find the file on your drive. I think the last step is fairly self explanatory. Hope that helps...

Hi Joe, I use good old s/r to determine when to jump off. Also, when MACD goes neutral (ie 0 line), its usually a good time to get off as price quite often changes direction or stalls, unless there are no barriers in the way of further price trend continuation. A lower/higher close on the smaller time frames builds up to a lower/higher close on the higher time frames, so discretion is paramount. I use good money management ie, 90% of good money management is getting in the trade at the right time, so my stops are quite tight. TP when the move runs out of steam.

I'm not even sure if this makes sense but to me it sure did, and that's what I'm going to do after I take a few days break off trading. It sure stinks to make 100% return and only to lose 50% to get back to where you were before.

--- 帖子 #1067 ---
I've been looking throughout this thread for various examples of using multiple time frames in our decision to enter a trade (such as the above example). It seems like a really good idea, but the problem is that when the multiple time frames are aligned, will the price have move up too much to be touching the 12 or 24 ema? Therefore it seems that we would rarely - if ever - will be able to enter a true CF trade.

If, for example on a buy trade, the time frames are aligned and the price dips back down to the 12 or 24 ema, then wouldn't at least 1 or more of the time frames be pointing downward and be out of alignment? By using the idea of trading when multiple time frames are aligned, then we would not be able to take the trade if it dips back to touch the 12 or 24 ema. I've see here on this thread to wait until the time frames are aligned and then enter when the 5 min chart is pointing upwards (as in a buy trade). However, at that point when the 5 min chart is pointing upwards then it most likely is not touching the 12 or 24 ema anymore. Isn't that true?

It's a "Catch-22" situation. We'd like to buy when the various multiple time frames are pointing upward, but when they are pointing upward then that most likely means the price has already moved up and away from the 12 and 24 ema. Do you guys see the dilemma?

--- 帖子 #1073 ---
I only post when I have something to say (though I check the thread daily.)

I trade for a living, and I incorporated Cornflower into my trading methodology because it is a solid dependable system.  The few losses I have had using the system are due to my interpretation of the charts, or to paraphrase Shakespeare, the fault dear traders is not in our charts, but in ourselves (yeah I know,...I'm going to English lit hell for that.)

The real beauty of Cornflower is it is simple to understand.  I am using it to teach my three youngest children (8, 10, and 12 years old) how to trade.  The older four are already out, and on with their careers and currently not interested in the markets.

Each one of the children has a demo account and when they become proficient trading on the demos, I will open a $300.00 mini account for each child.  The rules are simple.  At the end of each month, 50% of the profit goes into a savings account (to be rolled into a Roth IRA when large enough to do so) 25% is theirs to spend as they like, and the last 25% stays in the account (in order to increase the number of lots per trade.)  If they make bad trades and lose the account, a portion of their allowance will be held back to rebuild the account.

Watching the children working with Cornflower has been an enlightening experience.  They follow the rules and wait for the pull back to trade (they misread the charts at times, however, they are getting better with experience.)   They do not try to push the trade or jump early.  They just follow the rules...The way we all do,....right?

To get the answer to that question have a look at as many of these threads as you can. They all start out as great ideas and end up with everyone going onto the next big thing with one solitary voice inquiring "hello? Does anyone still trade this system?"

People like to think that they are smart and have made a discovery that will change the world. This is why 99% of Forex traders are simply losers.

Trading is not about finding the ultimate system that makes you heaps of cash. It is about being married to a boring screen day in day out making sure you are as strict as a catholic monk. Following your lame plan to the letter.

Then and only then will you make money. The smart ones get as far away from trading whenever they can and simply get it out of the way. Their a hundreds of systems that work out there. Do the backtests. But when you go to trade them live they don't work. Why?

Because they bore the pants off you! If you want to make money trading. Find a plan. Stick to it. Follow your trading plan to the letter. Stay away from Forums. They are full of losers that treat Trading more like playing poker machines than seriously making money. That's why they lose.

Find a system you like. Write a plan that calculates how much you need to invest to make so much a week based on a backtest. Don't be surprised when you make money. Expect it. Follow your plan and instead of hanging out with losers in forums. Sell it. You'll have much more fun than trading. I guarantee it

Taunted, the time to have taken that trade was two candles previous to your arrow.  You would have entered when the price was approaching the 24 ema.  Don't wait for the candle to close. The candle I'm talking about never touched the 24, but it came very close, which is why it's ok to pull the trigger as long as price is between the 12 and the 24.  If you would have done this and gotten out with 20 pips profit, it would have been a cornflower winner.  If you stayed in and got greedy, all profits would have soon been given back.

--- 帖子 #1102 ---
I set my stops between 50 and 100 pips (depending on the currency.)  That being said, if you have timed the entry correctly you should only see a reversal of 20 to 25 pips after entry.  Once I am in profit I move my stops up to keep my profit.  When moving stops the distance behind price is really dependent on the volatility of the currency at the time.  If it looks like a trend is running out of steam, then I keep my stop close.  If on the other hand the trend is strong, but whipsawing its way up (or down,) then I keep my stops farther out.  Setting targets of 20 or 30 pips and collecting is a solid way to increase your trading account.

Keeping a 1:1 risk/reward ratio is a good goal, however, it can also limit your profits.  Now before everyone starts screaming, let me explain my thinking.  If a trader consistently has 6 or 7 successful trades out of every 10 trades, he can with careful money management increase his account.  For example, if a person sets his stops for 20 pips and his TP for 20 pips, his risk/reward is 1:1.  Using the numbers from above we know we will hit the stop loss 3 or 4 times out of every 10.  That equates to 60 to 80 pips lost.  However, 6 to 7 successful trades equals 120 to 140 pips.  This gives a profit over the 10 trades of 40 to 80 pips.  Carefully increasing the number of lots as the account balance increases, will over a period of time develop the trader's income to the level he or she desires.  Being consistent and disciplined in one's trading will in time lead to success.  As I'm sure you have realized, it does not happen over night.

I hope my ramblings have been of help.

If I am trading multiple currencies, I use less lots per trade than if I were trading only one currency.

"Home run hitters drive Cadillacs, singles hitters drive jalopies."

Yes, one can be successful hitting singles, but the ones that REALLY go for it are the ones that REALLY hit it big! Just ask that guy who has been inducted in Cooperstown, N.Y. (home of the baseball Hall of Fame).

--- 帖子 #1157 ---
Hi,

Draw the date line (dotted vertical line) on your chart by right clicking on your chart and going to properties (bottom) and selecting "period separators". Also, google  and search for "MT4 Market Hours indicator and add it to your chart, which will give you visual market hours for Asian, London and US sessions with colored horizontal bars.

View the behavior of the pair of your interest over the past days in relation to the market hours or time of the day. You will then have a better assurance of the retrace for entries and also for exits.

It's often pays if you enter when market gets active and that is usually the  pre-open to few hours of each market session. Also note that trends often reverse in the afternoon. Further watch out for  the  market close  and the time of the day/ day of the week for new entries.

The above applies to any intra day trading method or strategy.

My view on your down arrow is, it will likely to be a nice retrace for "long", but not for "short". It's a Friday close and you should wait until the market opens on Sunday afternoon and follow the move there on.http://www.forexfactory.com/images/icons/icon7.gif

RS

--- 帖子 #1181 ---
Hi everyone - I'm the new guy

I've been a programmer since high school and this weekend decided to teach myself MQL4.  The Cornflower system seemed like a good project to learn with due to its simplicity.  I didn't see that anyone had posted an EA for it - if I've missed it, my apologies.  Hopefully I'm not stepping on anyone's toes here.

I hesitate to post the EA itself as it is still in its development stages.  If anyone that has experience with MQL4 wants to see it, they're welcome to PM me for it.  Backtesting shows some modestly successful gains over the past three months.  These gains are all based on trades of one lot at a time.

EURUSD - 753 pips

AUDUSD - 721 pips

USDCAD - 669 pips

USDCHF - 254 pips

These figures initially excited me, very much!!  But further examination tells me it can be better   Some notes:

1) While the EA is profitable, profitable trades occur only about 50-60% of the time.  Higher gains than losses compensate for this, however, I would like to refine the entry criteria.  More to follow.

2) I find that this EA works best with a currency that is strongly trending.  Even moderate choppiness (is that a word?) shows more losing than winning trades.  I added to the D1 chart EMA62, EMA200, and SMA800 (thanks Tiki) which improved this greatly.  I hope that fixing the point above will also help this.

Here's the entry strategy.  First, find the general trend direction.

if (EMA62 > EMA200 && EMA200 > SMA800) Direction = 1; // Uptrend

else if (EMA62 < EMA200 && EMA200 < SMA800) Direction = 2; // Downtrend

else return(0); // Choppy trend

Next, make sure the 72, 24, 12, and 8 EMAs are stacked properly.  (Reverse of this for a short of course.)

if (EMA72 < EMA24 && EMA24 < EMA12 && EMA12 < EMA8)

I have good luck with timing the entry using EMA24 and EMA8 on the M15 chart.  (Reverse for a short.)

if (EMA24_M15 < EMA8_M15)

Finally, I look to see if the bid has pulled back to the EMA12.

if (Bid < EMA12)

I've been experimenting with the angles of EMAs 8 and 24 on the M30 chart.  This seems to improve entries with some currencies, but not others.  Still debating whether to include this in the finished product.  (S1 and S15 refer to the parameter "Shift".)

if (EMA8_M30_S1/EMA8_M30_S15 > 1.0001 && EMA24_M30_S1/EMA24_M30_S15 > 1.0001 )

I exit when the EMA24 crosses the EMA12.

Well, there you have it.  I would MORE than welcome any and all comments that I could use to refine my criteria.  I'm mainly concerned with making the EA work in a choppy market...or at least recognize this fact and not trade.  Once it's done, I'm happy to post it...hopefully others can at least learn something from it.

Kindest regards,

Mango from British Columbia, Canada

--- 帖子 #1215 ---
Hi WARaintOVER,

Cornflower is a trend continuation system. If you refer to the first port by lever, he mentioned about all MAs used in Cornflower.

According to the rule, to initiate a position all MAs must line up approriately. For example, to go long, MA8 > 12>24>72. In an uptrend, wait for the price to bullback between MA12 and 24. Watch the price bounce from that consolidation range and thats were long position is taken.

CW

--- 帖子 #1225 ---
LOL!  If you could do that every time, you'd have the holy grail.

One thing you can do is wait to see whether the trend is resuming after the pullback.  You want a candle closing near the top or bottom of its range, and in the direction of the trend indicated by CF.   The candle must also be "real," i.e., a decent pip range.  In the Asian session you'll see candles whose range is less than 10 pips.  Ignore those.

Now, regarding Cornflower, i have a suggestion regarding trade entry. As we all already knew, there is no clear signal in Cornflower to enter a trade, it is based on trader own judgement. We all looking at the same thing with different perspectives. Pullback and trend continuation is subject to individual interpretation and we dont have specific "number" or quantity to justify our decision. So, what i'm trying to share here is to look at specific "condition" to happen before we open a position.

It is based on basic S/R. The idea is to enter once the S/R is broken and all Cornflower rules must agree. Attached is a recent USD/CHF with a nice downtrend. The yellow line is where the support got broken and also where we open a short position. I know we might miss some pips here, but i think it can save us from false entry.

--- 帖子 #1236 ---
As with any pull-back system, it seems that there is no definite point where a re-entry can be considered.  In other words, it's all purely discretionary, although I would bow to lever70 if she differs in her opinion regarding Cornflower!  For me, however, (and you, cyberwang, it seems), a less discretionary point of re-entry might make decisions a little easier.  Which is why I've been playing around with small TL's whilst demo-ing the system.  During a pull-back, I would usually wait for at least 3 candles before drawing the TL.  If the TL is broken inside the 8/12ema area, this can, a lot of the time but not always, signify the start of a decent move and well worth a trade re-entry.   However, if price has pulled back into the 12/24 or the 24/72 area, then regardless of TL breaks, for me it would definitely be a wait and see period.  I'd just prefer to handle TL breaks and re-entries around the 8/12ema zone, but that's just me.  Oh, and my re-entries would always be at the opening of a new candle after a TL break.  Trader's discretion will always (rightfully) be required, but anything that helps with his/her final decision  can't be bad, can it?

Cheers.

--- 帖子 #1250 ---
Trends start to build from the lower time frames.  I use the 5M TF for  confirming the trend on the 15M (the 15M is the TF I prefer to use for most of my entrance decisions.)

I like to see a strong trend on the 15M. I consider the trend to be fairly strong if the candle closes after crossing the 72 and the other three ema's are lined up in the direction of the trend (I also want to see at least two of the ema's have crossed the 72.)

I would suggest picking one or two currency pairs (GBP/JPY, GBP/USD, EUR/USD are good to start with) and following them for several months.  While the Weekly and Daily charts won't change much, the 4H, 1H, 30M, 15M, and 5M should give you a good feel for each individual pair.  You will find that after a while, some TF's will work better for your eyes than others (some traders make their decisions on the 5M chart while others use the Daily or Weekly, and you will find followers of every other TF in between.)   Purchase some notepads (I buy them by the dozen) and take copious notes.  The more you do now, the better it will be later.

I hope this was of some help.

--- 帖子 #1263 ---
I wait until the candle closes after crossing the 72 ema.  I prefer to see it close with at least 25% of the body of the candle on the closure side of the ema.

The direction and separation of the ema's are as important as the retracement.  If the ema's are lined up and headed in the same direction, then there is a better chance of the trend continuing.  If the ema's are bunched up and running flat or crossing over, the trend is not as strong.  The steeper the angle of the ema's the stronger the trend.  Also, the steeper the angle, the less the retracement.

When I first started looking at the Cornflower system, I put four charts up side-by-side (Hourly, 30M, 15M, and 5M.)  Each with the four ema's. I then studied the charts and their relation to price action.  Patterns start to stand out after a bit of study.

I hope the above was of help to you.

--- 帖子 #1266 ---
i understand your question dpfuller, this was my problem when i first started off with this system, it has something to do with your "feel" for the system which you tend to attain once you have spent some time with this system. for now you just need to know that you want the price to "settle" between the 8 and the 24 ema's which means it could be somewhere between 8 and 12, or maybe on the 12 or right at the 24 ema.

let me give you a few hints that will help you on your way

1) newly build trends will tend to pull back right off the 8 ema if the trned is strong and showing good signs of staying for some time.

2) mature trends will often find the support at the 12 ema or somewhere between the 12 and the 24 ema

3) exhausted trends will often look to sneak right through the 24 ema (represented by long wicks below the 24 ema by a candle or an actual close below it...note: the pull back mgith still occur but an entry at this stage will be riskier)

4) always enter at the start of the new candle don't be greedy, if you have missed the pullback candle look for other pairs, don't try to force your pips and squeeze them in your palm...they will work like fine sand, the more you press the more it slips through you fingers...

5) right so we enter at 00:00 of the new candle...?? wrong. you wait for atleast 5 mins of the 1 hour candle to see where the orice wants to go, again that helps in filtering some of the bad trades...if within 5 minutes you don't see a positve pullback sign wait further which will sometimes last the entire candle and we enter on the next candle

6) as a beginner keep the aggressive entry of this system out of your head, this is how i made majority of my losses when i first started off with this system....note: by new i mean new to the system and not to forex trading necessarily...

7) Look at multiple Time Frames pleeeeze!!!!! this may seem tiring, but it is very very important, you need to have all the four ema's on more then just the 30 min and the 1H Tf. i use it on the 4H and the daily too. once you do it you'll notice that all of these pullbacks and CF features also occur on these larger TF's....sometimes you see a clear trend on the 30 min and the 1H yet the price goes against you...why? many a times the price found the 72 ema on the 4H which was nowheer near the price in the lower TF's!!! there are many other times when you'll see that the price actually wants to follow the larger TF's as well so do use them.

8) if possible just do place another ema which is the 365 ema (applied to close) on all of these TF's....the reason is the price will "always" and no that's not an exaggeration...the price will always show respect to it, no matter what, if not right on it somewhere around it...it's very veryt powerful so do have this special ema to complement your 4 CF ema's too

i think that's it, as you go deeper into the system you'll see how good it is, and it has much more to it then just this....i.e the pullback entry and the aggressive entry. you can use it in many other ways and in every system!

Regards,

Ghous

After using the posted "rainbow" Multiple Moving Average (MMA) chart for several weeks, it appeared that it could be improved by adding Bollinger Bands, as referred to by lever70's postings regarding her M5 template.

The ForEx Factory has over 1,100 postings related to Bollinger Bands. It has been my observation that the price often stops at a Bollinger Band, in some time frame, prior to pulling back to a particular Cornflower line.

To save on ink, a template version with a white background was requested by a colleague.

Links to past writings by lever70 regarding Bollinger Bands:

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...er#post1426279

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...er#post1427698

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...er#post1429369

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...er#post1433438

ForEx Factory Site Search for Bollinger Bands:

http://www.forexfactory.com/sitesear...earchtype=site

The colors of the rainbow are Red, Orange, Yellow, Green, Blue, Indigo, and Violet.  ROYGBIV  "Roy G. Biv" and "Richard Of York Gave Battle In Vain"

Two MetaTrader 4 template versions are attached below.

That being said, the minute there are connection problems, missed stops and limits, or any other "technical difficulties", I will look for another broker.

--- 帖子 #1285 ---
Hi Lever,

Thanks for your feedback! I guess we are all glad that you are ok!!

Hope everything is fine and kicking! Welcome back and I would like to wish you the very best from beautiful Rio de Janeiro, Brazil!!!

Now, back to trading...

I know there's a lot of helpfull information about trading and so many different indicators, oscilators and systems. But from my short experience as an FX trader, I find that no other instrument is as helpfull as correctly drawing Support and Resistance lines.

"I have seen people draw trend-lines from about anywhere on a chart from different threads here @ FF.

So, allow me to put one strategy that might improve some of your drawings.

An uptrend is when demand exceed supply, and bearish visa versa.

So, how can we spot this events on our charts ?

A strong support (demand-line) is when you have 2 bars to the left (bear-bars) and 2 bars to the right (bull-bars) and resistance the other way around. Look for this to occur for the second time and apply a line between this 2 points you have. Candlestick pattern like hammer / invert hammer would help the creditability of your lines too.

Also correlate with different timeframes, don't get glued with only one timeframe !"

Drawing correct support/resistance lines, will you help you very much. This combined with the trend indicator (Cornflower is great for this), will expand your chances of trading the brake in a successful way. As the pull back "hits" one of the EMAs (considering the "maturity" of the trend) and it rebounds to resume the trend, once it breakes either the resistance or the support lines, go for the trade. It will resume strong and the break will provide for a good ammount of pips. Just be carefull when you leave the trade... Don't get over exciited because it will be tempting! The pressure is high once it goes your way.

Having said, I always look to place trades over the support/resistance lines that are in favor of the trend and specially after a pull-back. About an hour ago (13:00 EST) There was a strong pull back at CADJPY that came all the way from the 72 EMA! It was stong. I was a bit afraid of a turnaround, but once the pullback broke the resistance line... I knew I was in business. I went for 25 pips easily.

I find that Tom DeMark Trendline is a very helpfull tool. I also know that Lever mentioned this before... So I will attach an indicator that will suit all of you that wish to trade the break along with cornflower. Hope it helps.

Wish you all the Best.

Jupiter.

First of all, I'm only trading EURUSD at the moment. An excellent pair for noobs and non-noobs alike, with a small spread and relatively stable and predictable price action. I quite like it, being a former cable junkie. And it's really good for short-termers, too. Unfortunately, the cornflower chart for EURUSD is a mess right now. In times like these, the shorter-term strategies I outlined come in real handy, and I have made a lot of pips in the last two weeks using them. It's been nice rediscovering trading. Apparently, I still know a thing or two about it.

The intermediate trend is down on EURUSD, i.e., dollar-positive. As you know, I am not big on predictions. But I think this trend will continue, and then accelerate. I've been reading a lot of news and looking over long-term charts. My conclusion is that the end of dollar depreciation is near, if not already at hand. I will comment more on this soon. But the GBPUSD daily chart tells the story, soon to be replicated by EURUSD and then the other dollar currencies. (The parity party on USDCAD is done too.) There is a lot of chatter amongst government ministers in both the USA and EU, all of which amounts to a desire to see the dollar move higher.

Watch your dollar shorts closely; they are likely to be reaction moves. Of course, your charts should be the basis for taking trades. But I suspect our money this year will be made on dollar longs. Of course, to quote Jacko, "I could be wrong!"

--- 帖子 #1350 ---
No problem Adrian ... glad i can help out

Well if you look at that chart (post 93) and where the arrows are you will see that there is about 20 pips between them, now i wont speak for lever but if i recall somewhere in this thread she said that 20 pips is a nice profit (remember shes a scalper at heart, 20 pips would be huge to her ) so maybe thats why she put them there... as well as price is not rideing the top band as hard... im sure there are heaps of reasons but i guess you getting the idea?!

Take that 5 min chart in post 93, if the EMA's had crossed back over then i would jump out of the trade there. If they just turned up again then i would keep rideing untill they cross. Thats just me .... Im not always right.... others have other ways of trading this system that are just as good!

The longer term exit i like (but dont really trade cos who wants to be in a trade any longer then they need to be?)

is the 8 crossing back over the 12 EMA on the hour.

I also like risk/reward to be good, if i use a 20 pip stop im shooting for (but not locked into) a 30 pip profit target  ....... easier said than done!

Hope this helps

Bob

--- 帖子 #1429 ---
jdcompute,

Thanks for explaining your reasons for entry and exit. I had made the mention that I wasn't criticizing your trade because after I made the post, I realized it had the look of me questioning you of not following the system correctly, and of course that was not the case. There are times when we make a post that it comes across to the reader differently than we intended. Thanks for understanding.

As for the CF system, I've been following this system from the beginning when this thread started. Of the (demo) trades I've made, I've had good success. However, there have been 2 things that have been holding me back from really going full force and focusing totally on this top notch system.

1. Instead of picking a set way to trade the CF, I keep trying different ways to trade it. Such as: trying different time frames, entering on a pull back to the 12 ema, entering on a pullback to the 24 ema, entering on a pullback to the 62 ema, not waiting for a pullback but instead waiting for the MA's to angle/slope downwards or upwards, entering on a close of a candle, entering before the close of a candle, etc....

By doing all these things I am not getting any consistency with trading this system. It's also very time consuming. I need to choose a set way to trade and go with it!

2. The other thing that is slowing me down is that I keep looking at other systems and trying them out. It's basically me getting into the thinking trap of, "The grass is greener on the other side of the fence." This thinking has played a part in bogging me down.

I will say that having looked at many different trading systems, in my opinion, no system has yet to beat the CF system - when all things are considered. As I said, I'm always checking out other systems and when all is said and done, I continue to come back to the CF System. This system consistently performs well. Anyone can see this for themselves by doing backtests on it. There are other systems that do well but they are SO complicated! This is definitely not a problem with the CF system. The simplicity of the CF system is what sets it apart from most other systems. With it's consistent positive results, along with it's simplicity - and don't forget its relatively small stop losses (compared to many systems that require 50-100 pip or even larger stop losses)! - well, this system to me is hard for any other system to beat!

As I said, If I can get myself settled down, only focus on THIS system, and pick only ONE way to trade it, I'll probably suprise even myself of how well I can do with this!

Topgun

--- 帖子 #1449 ---
Sherlina,

Not sure this will help you but ill give it a go.

Early on (maybe even post 1) Felicia makes a point about the 8 crossing the 12 as a "get out" signal for longer term trades. I don't use cornflower that way but on the chart i attatch ill try and outline how someone might do just that.

I like the EMA's to all be stacked nice and in the right order, so the blue arrow shows a nice 12 EMA bounce and a great spot to get in short.

The red arrow is just on the candle after the 8 EMA crossed the 12 EMA so this saying to me the trend (for now) is retracing so a good spot to get out, taking that trade this way would have got you over 100 pips.

For me when the EMA's start crosing back over (on whatever timeframe you use) its time to sit on the fence, when its clear and stacked nice and clean its happy cornflower days.

Hope this helps

Bob

--- 帖子 #1485 ---
Jrex,

The short answer to you question is: The market only moves in 3 directions, up, down and sideways.

When the market is moving up or down thats a trend, cornflower is good at showing this because when the EMA's are lined up in the right order this shows a trend.

Sideways is when the market is range bound or not doing much trending.... in cornflowe thats when the EMA's are all bunched up and not showing a trend.

There is a lot more to this subject that you can (should) learn... a great place to start is babypips.com, they have a school system that shows all the basics of trading, a great place to fill in the blanks for people starting out.

Hope i have helped

Bob

--- 帖子 #1497 ---
kodflakes,

Thats not really the way cornflower works, when we see the EMA's cross over and start to spread out (where you took your entry) that is when we start looking and watching for the market to retrace back to one of the EMA's, once this has taken place and the market has started moving back in the direction we want to trade.. we enter.

take a look at  the chart of an AUD trade i took last night, notice the green tick is where the trend restarts and the red arrow is the candle that bounced almost on the 24 EMA, giving me my entry.

I think it's very good if people read post 1 again from time to time, i know i do and it keeps it all clear in my head, also the whole thread is a good read with lots of examples of how to trade cornflower.

kodflakes feel free to come back and ask any questions, a wise man once said to me "the only dumb question is the one you don't ask"

Hope this helps

Bob

--- 帖子 #1500 ---
Kodflakes, I use the Cornflower on 1 hour as my main trend. Like Bob says, wait for a pullback into the trend.  If you have to look to hard for a trend...it's not there. I trade off the 15 minute charts. I use a 12 and 48 ema as my trend direction and don't trade against it. I mainly trade E/J. Check out E/J and G/$ lately, strong trends. I wait for a pullback into the 1 hr CF trend and wait for the 15 min 12/48 cross to line up in the same direction. Ideally I wait for a small pullback to be safe and wait for the break of support or resistance. The reason I chose to wait for a cross on 15 min was because I was getting burnt placing an order at the 24 hourly. I asked myself why do some stop there and others don't. Answer: I don't know. So I came up with the 12/48 and it seems to work for me.

Hope this helps.

--- 帖子 #1511 ---
Really? I found that exits were not a problem for me, but entries were truly problematic. They are the main reason I abandoned this system months ago, after trying it for some (actually long) time in demo. Many others seem to have been quite successful with it, though, so the problem seems to be mostly mine.

The reason for not having problems with the exits is that I simply used to stick to a predetermined plan. Sometimes I left plenty of profit on the table and some others I waited a little too long and got nothing, but that's how it is. That part more or less worked for me. Entries, however... I still have nightmares. Leaving aside the fact that every once in a while you'll get the dreaded reversal (happens with almost any trend-following system and there is no way around it), I still found extremely difficult to time the entry properly. If I entered at the touch of the 12 EMA in a moderately strong trend, more often than not price would keep going to the 24 (and sometimes beyond) and stop me out. Dropping to the 5M timeframe helped, but by the time you see price is already bouncing back... well, it is already bouncing back, and you have lost the advantage of the "touch" entry, might as well have entered blindly on the bar before. I am sure you are familiar with this. For some reason, it seems my psyche is not well suited to this kind of "EMA touch" entry and I executed it very poorly, many of my cornflower trades were stopped out in the bar after the entry. Recently I had a long backtesting session of the system (wanted to see how it felt after months without using it) and it is still the same for me, I am unable to get the entries right.

Anyway, I am glad you are doing well with this system.

--- 帖子 #1516 ---
Pipadder,

It seems like you are finished trading the system and I am not sure if anyone else if trading like this but I can tell you a little bit about my own personal modifications...I was having a difficult time with entries as well because that is something that needs to be a "for sure" thing whereas exits I can figure out on my own.

So, what I've been doing is if the market is in a downtrend (EUR and GBP the past 12 hours) is placing a stop entry below the low of the candle that touches one of the EMA's. Now that doesn't filter every entry but it keeps my mind at ease in case the market continues to rally to the next EMA. Which did happen atleast twice today.

I do this completely on the 5m chart whereas the Hourly I enter on the touch of the EMA because there is just too many pips lossed if you enter short below that hourly candle.

Just my two cents but hope this helps anyone interested.

--- 帖子 #1533 ---
qwer2004,

First up i just want to make sure it's clear i was talking about a question from Christ. Jast and that question was:

"How long (and strong) should be trend to "safety" trade? - what do you think?"

Ok so i will assume that you have an idea of how cornflower works, if not go and read post one because all anyone needs to know to get started is there.

First when looking for a cornflower trade i need the EMA's to be stacked in the right order to show a current trend, the chart in this post shows a white circle around where the EMA's are bunched up and then starting to spread out in order - this shows me the start of a trend i may want to trade.

The 2nd thing i look for is has there been a trade already in this current trend? the way i trade is waiting for a pullback to either the 12 EMA or 24 EMA, in this chart the red arrow show the "first trade".

The 3rd thing i want and am now waiting for is a 2nd pullback (shown by the green arrow in the chart) if this pullback dose what i want and resumes the trend then i enter a trade.

Some people might say i am letting to many pips go, others might not like idea of waiting around when trade was there the first time... and thats fine but i know this works for me.

I hope this was clear... i'm not sure it was but let me know how your trading is going too!

Bob

--- 帖子 #1543 ---
Iceman,

That trade got me... it went and hit my stop before it went on down  so maybe my stop was to close? not really, thats the risk level i am happy with and they were HUGE candles so maybe i could just stay out the market if its like that!

Your spot on about moving stops and such, what i do now is something i got from the fokes over at the DIBS thread which is to set up the trade in 2 lots.

1st lot I set the trade up so the risk:reward is 1:1,

2nd lot I ride the trend and take profit where i always would, the great thing about this is once the 1st profit target is hit its a "free" trade as i lose no pips if i get stopped out and by not moving the stop to B/E the trade has room to move.

I know thats not what others will like to do but we all trade differnt ways

Bob

--- 帖子 #1547 ---
Bob,

On those 4hrly charts it is tough because stops have got to be very wide. I am glad to see you are incorporating two smaller lots. My profits have gone through the roof on the 5min chart because of it.

When it comes to risk:reward ratios - I don't get too hung up if my stop is 25 pips I have to take 25 pips profit initially. Setting things in stone is, in my humble opinion, not a place where a discretionary trader should be. Always analyze the charts and see what is best. You might realize that you should go for a smaller initial profit because the trend might be slowing down or whatever, but your stop might have to be a bit wider to accommodate the volatility of today's markets.

Just a thought as always. I hope that between the two of us we can try to keep this thread alive as it has benefited me beyond what most can understand. I might have to start my own thread to discuss my modified strategy and my own personal viewpoints.

Until then, trade with the trend and keep it simple. Trading is only made difficult if you make it that way.

God Bless.

--- 帖子 #1548 ---
Iceman,

The thing about wide stops is that i am just reducing the size of the trade, risking 3% of a your account with a 20 pip stop will mean more lots on the trade than if it was 3% at 100 pips.... we would hope that the 100 pip stop trade brings in more pips profit, but getting that stuff right is very important.

As a rule i place my stop above the high of the bounce i am trading... so far so go with this because in my experince cornflower trades go with me (and the trend) quickly and if price breaks above that level the maybe it was a bad trade anyway.

I am only on the 4 hour now because of time problems i am having at the mo, so still feeling my way with them. I am going to post a few select charts with some ideal and not so ideal trades from last week. (9-22-08 -- 9-26-08) My settings are just slightly different than the original. My EMA's are 16, 24, and 43. I stuck with the 24 because it seems to work quite well but I changed to the 16 and 43 because they have worked for me a bit better.

Attached is 2 Charts. The first is a EURUSD Chart from 9-22. There are blue boxes that I used to highlight each area where a trade can be attempted. I do not enter all of these because I am sleeping some of the times. Starting with the box to the far left which I will refer to as #1 and each box will be referred to as the next number in order. #1 is a good 24EMA Trade that I entered to the right side of the actual blue box.

This trade I entered and yielded +25 and +45 pips. #2 is a trade worth entering at either the 24 or 43. I was luckily asleep and missed that trade because it would have been a losing trade based on my parameters which is usually a 25 pip stop. #3, I was awake for and took but got in late. It obviously did not truly touch the 24EMA but with such a reversal bar off of that level I took the trade.

Another thing to keep in mind is that monday's are typically a trendy day with good profits for a system like this and that is also the reason why I took the trade. I would not have taken the trade any other day. I got +25 and +52 on that trade. At this point I quit for the day because I had two winning trades and there were any more trades until the #4 box. I did not take this even though I was watching because the trend was so far extended that I knew this was more of a risky pullback, in which it would have resulted in a loss. No EA can beat an open eyed discretionary trader with no greed.

Now on to the next day in the EURUSD (9-23-08) where the day was not as perfectly ideal. Not that you can't make good pips but knowing how far the market extended itself on monday, you must keep in mind that trades need to managed more diligently.

Box #1 is a perfect setup where the EMA's are "stacked" and there is a good trending market. I took a short at 4748, I believe, and took +20 and +42. My schedule is that I wake around 2-3am EST and if there is an opportunity I wait and take it. If nothing then I rewake at 5 and then 7. If the EMA's are in trending mode then I'll wait up but if not then I go back and sleep. Once NY session is open I am up all day because I also trade the grain markets.

Box #2 is a trade that I was not awake for because I had taken profit earlier but this is a perfect setup that just didn't work out. Either EMA would have resulted in a loss but this is no problem at all. We are merely trading with the odds that over time we will come out on top.

Box #3 is also a trade that I was not awake for and quite questionable as to whether there was profit. If you would be going for +20 then you would have gotten your initial but then break even on the second position. If you went for 25 to 30 then I believe you would have taken a double loss. Nevertheless, it was a good set up once again.

Box #4 is a trade entry that I missed by 1 pip. I place limit orders and move them every 5 minutes so that I can take advantage of moves like this that are only at the price level for an instant which is difficult to stare at the screens like that for so long. That trade would have yielded +25 and +0 if taken.

Box #5 is a trade that I did enter and got me worried at one point with the price spike. Haha. I place my stops at -25 though so it never hit. I did get +25 and +43 on that trade. A very choppy market at the time which is difficult because ultimately the day fell much harder. No worries though because you can't predict anything...all you can do is follow a system and not regret missing out on things.

I hope this helps anyone trying to find a system that works. Any questions are welcome as I am sure I skipped some things and maybe some would like to dig deeper into how I make certain decisions.

God Bless.

--- 帖子 #1602 ---
Qwer,

My decision to take profit is based off of a few things. First is if there is a pivot line close I will take profit a bit short of that. Second, on monday's there is usually more follow through for whatever reason so I will be more patient and take profit at a higher level. Third, I take profit on both positions at +25 when I have had somewhat of a losing day and just need the pips and the market isn't really following through. That has burnt me though because sometimes the real trends happens in the NY afternoon which is my favorite time to trade because there is less whipsaw volatility.

I take most positions at the 24 ema but I have changed a couple of things and have mentioned these sparingly. I don't really trade the GBPUSD much anymore except on monday's because there is more trending movement BUT I still compare what is going on in the GBPUSD with the EURUSD.

That is because if, for example, there is a downtrend and both are retracing I will take a look over to the GBP. If the GBP has already broken the 24 and 43 to the upside then I will move my entry on the EUR to the 43. That way I know that I have a less chance of getting stopped. I don't really reference this too often in my descriptions so I thank you for asking that great question.

God Bless you too and I hope I answered your questions fully.

--- 帖子 #1626 ---
Aarangio,

No problem with the questions...the more we ask the better we all become!

Yes, I use a 25pip stop on all positions. It is what has worked for me on the 5min chart. Just enough room for volatility, tight enough to keep losses to a minimum, and easy to remember.

I do trade with 2 lots. I always take the initialy profit at +25 and then move my stop to break even for the other position. At that point I decide on recent S/R, pivots, and sometimes just an eye for the chart for my exit. The big negative with 2 lots is the double loss when you do take a loss. So you need to be adjusting your money management for a 50 pip loss and not 25.

I cut my trade equity in half so that I was trading the same amount but in a dual entry format. I have been contemplating going back to a single position for some time but I have too much regret when I see a nice move for 50 or more pips after my entry. Personal preference is very important and the ability to self-analyze so that you can reach a positive conclusion is what each individual trader needs to do.

I only trade the EUR but I do trade the GBP on mondays because I recognized there seems to always be a nice trend on monday.

Box #8 I entered at 1.34381 and placed my stop at 1.34131. The low was 1.34154. I took initial profit at 1.34631 and my second take profit was at 1.34970. That missed by .9 of a pip. I cannot remember exactly why I chose 1.34970 but there must have been some justification!

I enter at the 24EMA at all times EXCEPT when the GBP hasn't retraced at all yet. Then I sometimes will wait for the EUR to go to the 43 and that is usually when the GBP is reaching the 43. Vice versa - Sometimes the GBP is already at the 43 so I know the enter immediately at the 24. That is not set in stone because both operate fairly independently.

The only time I would trade with a confirmation style is if there is a strong trend and I want to find a way to enter. I will wait for a retrace to the 16. Place a stop entry on the opposite side of the candle that touched and see if I get filled. For a short I would place a sell stop below the low of the candle that touched the 16. I dont really do that anymore becaues there are enough retraces for good trades at the 24 and 43.

I hope this answers all of your questions!

God Bless.

This thread needs to be back up top because this is one of the most powerful threads in all of Forex Factory.  Felicia is a brilliant woman with powerful insights into the market.  This system is still pure gold, as laid out in post number one.  The method is as powerful as it gets.

My advice to you is POSITION SIZE!!!!  This is what works for me... 100 pip loss=2% of your capital.  For a $5000 dollar account you trade 1 mini-lot.  DO NOT VIOLATE THIS RULE.

Also, what I use for a stop is a visual one.  I do not use a pre-set stop-loss (aka 'target for your broker to take out').  My stop-loss is: if there is a 1HR bar close past the 72EMA against my position, it is a loss.  You will notice in Cornflower that after a big move, the first return to the 72EMA is a very strong support. The 72 is the line in the sand.  If it closes past it, you lost this trade, look for your quickest exit.  LET THE BAR CLOSE and then make a decision.  It is an emotionless process.

For PROFIT, I look for recent lows/highs and I also use Bollinger Bands for reasonable exits.  DO NOT BE GREEDY!!!  Leave the top and bottom 15% for the risk-takers.  We don't need that, just take the meat off the bone and go home.

Another huge thing is this... jump up to the 4HR chart and use the same EMA's as the 1HR and determine the 4HR trend.  Your 1 HR Cornflower entries must match the 4HR trend!  NO EXCEPTIONS!!  If the 1HR says go long, but the 4HR is short, you have NO TRADE.

I will be lurking around for awhile, so if there are any Cornflower specific questions you have, I would be glad to help anyone attempting to learn the finer points of what has been presented so far.

--- 帖子 #1647 ---
it's not just brokers, topgun, it's the whole industry.  it's obvious where some stops will be placed by the majority of traders, and the big fish in the sea will try to take those stops out.

When I say I use a visual stop it is this -  If the 1 HR bar closes past the 72, it is a loser and I will close the trade manually, AT A LOSS, when it returns to the 24.  I only acknowledge BAR CLOSES with this method.  Go back and backtest and see how many wicks break the 72 without there being a close past it, or how many S/R levels are 'broken' only to have it return in the direction you planned on.  I set Take Profits on every trade.  I do not set stop losses.  If my trade identifies itself as a loser, I move the Take Profit to the next reasonable exit area and let the trade close itself out.  This is how I minimize my losses.

This is the most powerful realization of my last month - using the bar close past the 72 as my indicator that this trade is a loser.  The other one is that I have finally dialed in the position size using my 100 pips = 2% rule.  I rarely lose 100 pips, but this has been pure gold for me, I can handle the drawdown that occurs with this method.

--- 帖子 #1653 ---
this is something I am currently working on.  I'm glad you brought it up.  Yes, the most conservative thing to do is close the trade the moment the bar closes past the 72.  I highly recommend this.  It is the easiest way out and is emotionless and requires no thought.  It closes past 72, IT'S A LOSER, close the trade!

However, if you have used Bollinger Bands, you will notice an inevitable return to the midline, which is a 20 SMA, which is very close to the 24 EMA in value.  So when the bar closes past the 72 EMA and I know I have a stinker of a trade, I don't just panic and close it, I instead look to the midline Bollinger Band, aka the 24 EMA, and I set my Take Profit to be at that level (most likely closing out at a loss), and wait for price to make it's natural return there.  Basically I am alway letting price come to me.  Go and backtest and see that price ALWAYS returns to these averages.  The averages may be higher/lower than you'd like when price finally gets there, but the fact is, price ALWAYS returns to it at some point.  So you might as well just set your trades to close out at those levels.  You control the trade, do not let it control you.  Look, see and set limit orders and take profit levels, shut the computer off and walk away for a few hours, come back and reevaluate.

The reason I can trade this way is my POSITION SIZING. I trade with the right amount to handle the drawdown that occurs. My 2% of my account=100 pips rule is pretty golden, though slightly aggressive.  1%=100 pips is better for beginners I'd say.
