--- 帖子 #1692 ---
Can  you help us explain what the "actual", "forecast" and "previous" numbers mean in the calendar? What do those numbers represent?

--- 帖子 #1693 ---
Previous - the number last time the report was released.

Forecast - the consensus on what the upcoming number should be

Actual - the news number itself. Deviations from the forecast will move the market on a red news release.

Do not be in the market at news time unless you are already in a long term position. Brokers widen spreads, and you will find yourself in a bad spot.

Do not try and guess what the number will be. That's gambling, pure and simple. News can move the market 100 pips or more in a very short period of time. Also, do not trade news using an autoclick program. That was a good game a couple of years back, but brokers have long since gotten hip to it.

We have to be aware of when the news comes out to protect ourselves. You can attempt to trade the move after the spike, once spreads have returned to normal. This can be accomplished using my 5/10 system that I outlined earlier in the thread. Don't worry too much about the news itself. As I've always said, just trade with the market.

--- 帖子 #1695 ---
Looking back through some recent posts, I'm seeing a lot of indicators being added. I've always made a point of saying that traders shouldn't rely so heavily upon indicators, and I still feel this way. If indicators make you feel more comfortable about taking a trade, then pick just one and stick with that one only. But you are really better off without them.

Indicators are derived from price. As such, they lag what price is actually doing. You are much better off trading on price action.

Yes, EMAs are indicators. But I've found that they are the least of all evils. They represent the movement of price over time, and price tends to gravitate back toward a mean. This is why Cornflower works.

Indicators other than moving averages, in my opinion, are largely voodoo. They lull traders into a false sense of control over events and distract us from paying attention to what price is actually doing. We get paid only if we are right on price. Cornflower aims to gauge price direction.

The only other indicators I've used are (a) bollinger bands on my 5/10 chart to gauge volatility, and (b) cross-currency correlations. I haven't discussed correlations here, but they are invaluable. Typically, EURUSD moves with GBPUSD, and they are opposed by USDCHF and (to some extent) USDJPY. So if USDCHF is going up, GBPUSD and EURUSD should be going down.

Even if you only trade EURUSD, you should watch the other pairs. If the point of indicators is to predict the future, then we should be watching all four of these pairs at once. More often than not, when the GBPUSD moves, the EURUSD follows, and the USDCHF goes in the other direction. It's usually cable that moves first, though this is not always true. The point is, more often than not one currency pair will tell us where the others are going.

Go to http://www.mataf.net and look at the correlation tables, which are updated frequently. They will help you in making your trading decisions.

--- 帖子 #1697 ---
I don't have much to add at the moment.  But trade vigilantly and protect your profits.

We are in the midst of a financial crisis whose outcome is far from clear.  Liquidity is thin because market participants don't trust one another.  Remember that the forex market is comprised primarily of banks, and they are all playing defensive right now.  There is an unwillingness to commit capital, and a general sense of mistrust.  In illiquid markets, the moves are sudden and swift, and can't be easily predicted.  As I type this, I am watching the EURUSD zoom up 40 pips in an hour, with violent downswings along the way.  This type of action never used to happen in the early hours of Asia trading.  It is now near-routine.  There are, of course, opportunities in this kind of action.  But be careful.  Trade what you see, and guard yourself against trading on expectations of how things "should" happen.  The past is the past.  We are in a different era than we were a year or even six months ago, and everything is suspect.

I am currently using Cornflower as a means to gauge (oh look, EURUSD just dropped 15 pips) general market sentiment, but am relying on my shorter-term systems for actual trades.  I'm willing to take any and all questions relating to these.  Mind you, they are not for the faint of heart.  Then again, trading isn't more generally.

Over and out,

F

--- 帖子 #1717 ---
I have been using the CF H1 MA settings on H1 and M30 TFs and the M5 MA settings on M5 only. I have added STARC bands and Fractals (for a bit of convinience) and ZigZag. I like mutlitimeframes gearing, since M5 to M30 is a 1 to 6 time ratio. I also use Cf as originally designed to H1 TF, and pay attention to the performance of the 72EMA. I trade only GBP/USD and it is possible to scalp both ways in relation to the direction of the EMA72 on H1, but going against it demands a tighter SL and taking smaller profits. Going in the direction of this 72EMA on H1 allows one to miss the smaller cycle/s and still come out with profits, as the trend on a larger TF is less likely to change.

Best wishes to all and many good trades,

--- 帖子 #1754 ---
This has come up again here and in other places. Regarding a Cornflower EA, I devised Cornflower as a discretionary system, and I think it's best traded that way. No computer can replicate the judgment of an experienced, disciplined trader. There have been a number of attempts to automate Cornflower but no one has yet succeeded in devising an EA that is truly workable. The problem with Cornflower is that it's a trend-following system, and if every entry is taken there are going to be periods of drawdown in ranging markets. There is no way around it. Sure, we can write an EA with fixed profit targets of 20 or 50 pips, but the profits that result will mostly be eaten away by the inevitable losses in unfavorable market conditions. It's not the fault of the system. The market is unstructured and does not obey one set of rules at all times. As traders, we have to adapt to prevailing conditions, and adjust our decisions accordingly.

That said, I encourage further work for those up to the task. I think any EA that incorporates Cornflower would need to be adaptive to market conditions, taking into account short- to mid-term fluctuations in volatility, average daily range, and multi-currency correlations. We'd also need to take into account support and resistance on multiple time frames, which is difficult to code with reliability. Pivot points are often cited as a solution to this problem, but I have found their usefulness illusory.

I'm glad interest in the system is still strong after all this time.   February was a frustrating month for those trading the USD pairs, but rewarding to those who traded long XXXJPY.  The market will find its bearings before too long.

--- 帖子 #1771 ---
Hey Bob!

Good eye for the charts. You might just be converted someday to the lower times frames. My setups are a little bit different because of the different time period ema's but all in all it is very close.

I wanted to comment on the comment that you made concerning the crossing of the 72 or in my case the 43ema...

I have personally found that there is a losing trade that preceeds this happening (obviously because price broke down and did not continue on the trend). When price breaks through the 43ema, the shorter ema's are typically stacked correctly on the downside (in this case) and then what I have found is a high probability trade when price FIRST retraces to the 43ema.

Typically the shorter term ema's are close to the longer term ema when this happens so you have a ton of resistance from 3 ema's all at once.

This chart I posted gives 2 examples:

Box #1 is a failure and a losing trade. But Box #2 is a retrace afterward that does end in a profitable trade atleast for me. Notice the ema's are all at one place. Not real text book because of all that volatility but it got the job done.

Box #3 is a losing trade that was quite the nice setup. Box #4 is a trade that I took on the short side and gave plenty of pips. This example is more textbook because I don't like too many bars to print before this retracement happens or I feel like it is more like violent whipsaw action than anything. (that statement relating back to boxes #1 and #2)

I hope this helps and it will get you in on some early trend reversals from a true trend retracement.

God Bless.

Hi everyone, I have some good news! A Cornflower EA has finally been created! I think this is the very first Cornflower EA posted in this thread that automatically takes the trades for us! I did see another EA here, but it just gave arrows and audio alerts of trade setups, but it did not take the trades automatically...it required the trades to be taken manually. However, this EA takes trades automatically.

Earlier this week I posted in the "Programming Discussion" section of FF a thread requesting someone to make an EA for our wonderful Cornflower system. Only one person was kind enough to agree to make the EA for us ... and he was nice enough to do it for free. His name is Postrock and I want to thank him for making this EA for us. Thanks Postrock!

I will say, however, that I have not yet tested it ... so I hope I'm not being too premature in posting it here right now. I just want to let everyone know that an EA is available right now and I wanted to give everyone an early chance to test it.

With this EA you have to set your own stops and targets. You also have to set your own timeframe and your number of lots you want to trade. You can also choose any of the Cornflower ema's you want as the trigger ema (the ema you want a trade to enter on when it touches).

Even though I still think trading manually is probably the best way to trade this system (or any system for that matter), I think it is worth a try to see if an EA can actually be profitable. I figure there's no harm in trying (just be sure to test it thoroughly with a demo account before using a live account).

--- 帖子 #1775 ---
I'm really suprised nobody here has not said anything at all about the Cornflower EA that has finally been developed.

As I remember, throughout this thread there were several people asking for an EA to be used for the Cornflower system. Now we got one and nobody seems to care.

For those that care about it, here is some info about it and how I am using it:

I am currently trading on 2 demo accounts – FXDD and Interbank. I was using Alpari but I decided to drop it and focus on the other 2 demo accounts.

(I am editing in the below part because for some reason it did not go through when I originally posted this message).

I am trading the 5 min chart on FXDD. I am trading only with the eur/usd with the 5 mn chart. I am testing a 15 pip SL and 30 pip target. I am using the 12 ema for the trigger (entry).

WIth the Interbank platform I am trading the Cornflower on the 1 hr chart. I am testing a 30 SL and 60 target with most currencies. With the gbp/jpy I am using a 40 SL and 80 target. I decided to use the 8 ema (instead of the 12 ema) as a trigger for the 1 hr trades. Since the EA will currently take only 1 trade at a time, I have several currencies set up with the EA. This gives me better odds that it will almost always be in a trade. Because when one trade ends, hopefully another will happen very quickly.

Currently we have 2 minor problems with the EA:

1. The rules state the ema's need to be in an angle for the best results for a trade. RIght now the EA wil enter all Cornflower set-ups whether or not they are in an angle. Last week I asked Postrock (the developer of the Cornflower EA) if he can make it for the ema's to be in a 20 degree angle for the trades. He said maybe he can do it this week.

2. It looks like the EA will take no more than 1 Buy trade and no more than 1 Sell trade at a time. This basically means it won't take more than 1 trade at a time (unless you are trading with more than 1 demo account ... as I am doing. Then you can take 1 trade on each demo account). Postrock said he plans on fixing it so we can trade with several currencies instead of just one.

I hope he can get these problems fixed. Postrock has done a good job making the Cornflower EA. If he can fix these problems, then I will really be excited about it.

Topgun

Topgun

I care.... I am not with an mt4 broker and so even if I wanted to I can not use it.

To often when someone makes an EA for free people will say but it wont do this or can you change it to do that?

I am not asking for these things to be changed or for any new EA to be made but just saying what I see as problems with it for me.

The angle thing may be something people use but by the nature of how Cornflower works when the EMAs are lined up the market will have been running and some angle will be present, I know they can flatten out when things are quite but often that will mean they are jumbled up and I'm not looking to trade in that situation anyway.

Also one of the ways I enter a trade is by using the high/low of the bounce candle to enter, this means (at least some of the time) that trend has resumed and the market is showing this by moving back away from the bounce EMA, having this filter means not always getting in at the best price but also not getting stopped out every time price just keeps going the other way.

Also what about Lever's 5min entry, also a good filter?

Hope this helps

Bob

--- 帖子 #1792 ---
Postrock,

I'm just letting you know your new EA appears to be working correctly. It has taken many trades from many different currencies - with many trades running at the same time - just as it is suppose to.

As I mentioned from my previous post, I've been away from my computer (and had it turned off) since last Thursday. I returned home late yesterday afternoon and set up my computer to try the improved version of your EA. I have 2 demo accounts - Interbank for 1 hr chart trades and FXDD for 5 mn chart trades. Here are my settings for each account:

Interbank

Time Frame: 1 hour
Trading Time: 24 hrs a day
Number of currencies I am trading: 10
Bar: 0 (I do not fully understand how the "Bar" number affects a trade, so I just left it on "0".
MA Trigger: 6 EMA (I am testing the 6 ema as the trigger because it always seems to work better for me than the regular CF ma's)
Stop Loss and Take Profit: 30 SL & 60 TP for 9 out of the 10 currencies (the exception is the gbp/jpy of which I have a 50 SL & 100 TP)
trading direction: Long & Short

FXDD

Time Frame: 5 min.
Trading Time: from London Session open at 3am est to U.S. close at 5pm est
Number of currencies I am trading: 10
Bar: 0 (I have the bar at this number for the reason mentioned above).
MA Trigger: 12 EMA (I decided here to use the most commonly used CF ma trigger)
Stop Loss and Take Profit: 15 SL & 30 TP for 9 out of the 10 currencies (the exception is the gbj/jpy of which I have a 20 SL and 40 TP)
trading direction: Long & Short

Keep in mind that I am only testing these settings. I plan to test different stop losses and take profits, and I plan to test in order to find the best MA trigger. I also plan on testing other aspects of the Cornflower system. Another good thing to test is the "trading direction" setting (the setting is called "positions" on the EA). Right now I have my 2 demo accounts set to take all Long AND Short trades. Actually, I think the smart thing to do is to make the best estimate of the most likely direction the market is going and set the setting for that direction (example, set it "Long" if you think the market is going up for a particular trading day or session).

So far in the 1 day of trading with the new EA, I have had more losses than wins. I haven't exactly calculated the dollar amount result, but it is negative amount for the 5 mn chart account, but positive amount (in profit) for the 1 hr chart account.

But remember, I am totally in testing mode right now, and also it has been only 1 day of testing for me. So don't read too much into those results.

Topgun

--- 帖子 #1800 ---
Glad to know someone else that is on the 5m charts.

I have my ema's at 16, 24, and 43. Those have worked best for me since late last summer. I wait for them to align/stack in a direction and wait for a pullback to the 24. I will take that position but if I miss it I will take an entry at the 43 if it retraces that far.

I do NOT wait for any candle to close. I enter at the moving average.

My stops are typically at 25 pips. I will place as close as 20 and as far as 30 pips. This is more of a gut thing and by that I mean when I look at the chart does 20 look way to close? Does 30 pips look way too far away from entry? On more volatile days 20 will look so darn close that you know you are going to get bumped. I don't do a stop any bigger than 30 because I usually don't go for much more than that on the profit side.

I take all position off of table at one exit point which is typically 20-30 pips profit. I did trade before where I scaled off to try to catch a bigger move but I realized that there is a double loss and you have to make that back up with twice as much profit. It gets too complicated at that point.

I do like to target pivot points sometimes or significant S/R. Also, I will take a look at the hourly cornflower chart to see if I can target a close, longer term EMA. So, there are times when I do let a position go for much more profit but not that often.

Hope this helps.

God Bless.

--- 帖子 #1826 ---
Judging from your journal, it seems you're doing an excellent job of managing trades.  It just takes patience and experience to know when to take a profit, as opposed to letting it run further.  I still get tripped up sometimes myself.  Letting your profits run is actually harder than cutting a losing trade.  With a loser, you know the trade is over.  But a winning trade can keep producing pips.

When I went about developing Cornflower, my goal was exactly this: how can I get 20 pips with relative ease?  Most of the time, the system will give you those pips if you follow the rules.  Of course, the market may retrace and generally yank your chain before it hits that target, which is why we have to be patient and also not over-leverage ourselves.  Too often we get scared out of trades that are viable because of short-term market gyrations (what I call "spaz").  If we're trading from the 1H, we need to give a trade a few hours to properly develop, and abide by our stop.  And then we move that stop in the direction of our trade if it works out.  Again, it takes some guts to do this.  Only with hard screen time can one get a sense for the mood of the market, and then act accordingly.

Well, I just completed an exhausting move from Chicago to LA.  Finally starting to settle in here. But I've had no time to follow the market of late.  I hope to have more time going forward.

That said, I don't post much to the thread anymore because after nearly 2 1/2 years I've more or less said all that I can say about this system.  I still use it myself, and I'm glad this thread is still active.  The system still works, provided you follow the rules and don't start adding unnecessary indicators (which I've found mostly useless).

The only thing about this system that could be hammered out in more precise detail is when to take profit and/or loss, but I've found that there are no hard and fast rules that can be hammered out as with the entry.  Cornflower can be used to either set up a scalp trade or a mid-term swing trade, and I pretty much left it up to you guys to discern what works best for you.  I can assure you that there's no "secret" I've omitted.  I more or less use Cornflower to gauge trend, and then move to the 5-min to enter.  I've always been more of a scalp-type trader at heart, only because I don't like sitting around and waiting.  If I have a profit I like to take it sooner rather than later, though on occasion I do the swing trade for 50+.

Don't force your trades.  Wait for a proper setup, and when it's there, take the trade.

Cheers,

Lever

ps - I get these PMs from time to time asking me answer questions on Skype.  Sorry y'all, but I have no time for private tutoring, and much prefer my anonymity in cyberspace.

--- 帖子 #1882 ---
I don't use that 15-minute entry I briefly spoke about early in the thread.  It was a brief experiment that I discarded.  I just use the hourly Cornflower setups in conjunction with the 5-minute, and I do this more or less as I did 2 1/2 years ago.  The only thing I don't really use much anymore is the Bollinger bands on the 5-minute, only because it's another thing to look at and I don't really like distractions.  If anything, my trading has become simpler.  I just look for pullbacks and I watch the character of the price action.

Folks, don't fret over the market.  Yes, the market has been challenging over the past year, perhaps more than usual.  But the market challenges us year after year anyway.  It's going to do what it's going to do.  All we need to do is follow the movement of price, and this is what Cornflower does.

--- 帖子 #1883 ---
Hi Bob, thanks for your continuing efforts to keep this thread alive.  I appreciate the charts you post on a regular basis.

Your question points to something I long ago lost interest in, namely predicting what the market is going to do.  No one knows.  All I care about is making a judgment call on what it is likely to do in the very near future, and by that, I mean in the next hour to few hours.  Sometimes we are lucky to happen upon a move that lasts for days or even weeks, but the only way to get lucky in this way is to skillfully observe what is happening right now.

If price is acting funky and I'm down a few pips, I get out.  If I'm up a few pips and it looks as if it's going to keep going, I stay in.  If it stalls, I get out.  Pretty simple stuff.  I don't do the longer-term trades often, only because I don't have the personality for it.  Also, I have other interests besides trading and I like to pursue them.  I simply don't want to have to worry about what that silly Euro is doing every minute of the day.

So.  How do I know what it "looks" like it's going to do?  From my experience of watching the market.  I've been trading forex for several years now (with some long breaks from time to time).  Watching price action is an art that takes lots of screen time to hone.  I've spent countless hours in the dead of night watching the ways in which price moves, and I've developed a feel for different kinds of market conditions.  Unfortunately, I've never been able to systematize this in a way that I can explain here.  It's something that each trader has to learn for him or herself.   Sometimes this feel leaves me for a time, much in the way athletes find themselves in a slump.  I just have to trade my way out of it.   But there is no contradiction between having trading rules and having a feel for price action.

I hope this post makes sense...

--- 帖子 #1972 ---
Hi Chace,

I don't follow the GBP/JPY so I wont comment on that pair. I have taken a 1 hour chat of the USD/JPY and blacked out all the candles after the hammer in question (I'm no artist ) to give a better picture of what you might have been seeing yesterday.

I think there are lots of things to take into consideration before placing a trade, some of the things I noticed about this set up were:

That the pull back was not clean and standalone meaning that the candles before it where next to it and the hammer was in there shadow of those candles so it was not a true pull back in my opinion. Also the candles before the hammer are "allover" the EMA's

There is a "whole number" not far above and you would be trading into that zone, the market had tested that level twice in the two hours before the hammer setup and had been rejected both times.

I could not see an easy way into this trade using the 15 or 30 min time frames

Just a few of my thoughts.

--- 帖子 #1973 ---
I can't see any good setups right now during the euro open so I thought I might just indulge myself and give a point or two I feel are important to keep in mind when trading.

First thing is that I try not to chase trades I wait for them to come to me. Not always easy to do but the good setups stand out and I want to be trading only these good setups.

Which leads me to the next thing... patience, everyone who's trading needs it and even more so with Cornflower. Trades wont always be there everyday and you sometimes just have to chill out and wait for the market to sort its self out.

Just something to think about.

--- 帖子 #1975 ---
Chace, I don't know how may pairs you follow but it can be worthwhile looking at some extra pairs. There are two theories about this that are applicable to any type of trading...

1. Trade only 1 pair until you are very good at it, know the pair well, trade the pair well.

2. Trade a system (or even better one type of setup) when there is a setup because you know it so well you will trade it well.

--- 帖子 #1976 ---
Yes I agree Bob, either one of the other. I personally watch 7 pairs so one setup is definitely most suited.

I think with Cornflower on the one had the best trades may be soon after the cross because you are likely getting in at the beginning, however this can obviously result in false direction and on the other hand once there is a clear trend going you are trading with a clear directional bias after seeing it move, but then again it is likely you are getting in at the end. Combining other factors and only taking the clear setups seems to be the best approach which definitely requires patience.

Have you been trading this consistently or is it just casual as I've seen you've been posting on this particular thread for over 4 years!

--- 帖子 #1977 ---
Hi Chace, I don't want to get to self indulgent and give everyone my life story but yes I have been trading Cornflower for a long time. As I talked about above there are times when it seems like nothing is doing and no trades are able to be taken, I do muck around with other ideas to fill in the down time between Cornflower trends. Someone said earlier in the thread that Cornflower is slow at making money and while this could be true I have found because of its simplicity that it performs well over a long period of time. Also I have a philosophy that the process of success is boring... as an example an athlete who wins a gold medal may be excited at the time that they won as they should be, but its the years and years of training, getting up early, eating correctly that nobody sees which lead to the success, its not by chance. In that way success could be considered boring

--- 帖子 #1978 ---
That's useful to know Bob, I guess patience really is a virtue when it comes to trading. The likelyhood of each pullback being successful after the 24-72 cross becomes less and less likely so it is probably best to just trade the first pullback and then any subsequent pullbacks to the emas should only be taken if it is a very obvious potential reversal point or you see a hammer or something.
